    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_ab9a3bbf-e730-455e-bbfb-e9be1c98d139'

<span id="freeTextContainer840648546589430153">I cannot believe that this is it... <br/><br/>I'll miss my apple-eating Shinigami. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1462724630ra/19035688.gif' width='400' height='500' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I cannot believe that this is it. <br/><br/>I cannot say much about this one because the first twenty pages killed me. <br/><br/>This series gave me so many great characters to love. I had to love Kira even though he is the villain and mass murderer. I love Misa (not only because she's my namesake) but because she was who she was. She was the girl who loved a boy who did not love her back and only used her. She lived blissful life thinking he </span>
  <span id="freeText840648546589430153" style="display:none">I cannot believe that this is it... <br><br>I'll miss my apple-eating Shinigami. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1462724630ra/19035688.gif" width="400" height="500" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I cannot believe that this is it. <br><br>I cannot say much about this one because the first twenty pages killed me. <br><br>This series gave me so many great characters to love. I had to love Kira even though he is the villain and mass murderer. I love Misa (not only because she's my namesake) but because she was who she was. She was the girl who loved a boy who did not love her back and only used her. She lived blissful life thinking he loved her back. And she was a ball of energy which was hard to control!<br>I loved Mello because he was neither the good guy nor a bad guy. He only wanted to be better than Near, and in the end, he was because he became the last key to succeeding. <br>I loved Matt who was hardly there and yet I had to love him and wish there was more of him. I still hope that Matt and Mello would get their own series.<br><br>I knew this would happen and Ryuk said it right away that he would do it. <br><br>And yet here I have to say something about one theory. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[What if Near used the Death Note. What if when he got the real one, he wrote down that Mikami would come and do what he did and not suspect that his Death Note is fake and then commit suicide. It is very possible. Or maybe I just don't want Near to win this easily. I can agree that Light might have missed this possibility and he was supposed to lose. But still... This is not how it ends in my mind.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>And I have to wonder how different it would be if Ryuk was more like Rem or if Rem was alive?</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_1689837269" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1689837269" />
    <a title="Apoorva" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25605420-apoorva"><img alt="Apoorva" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597844654p2/25605420.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1689837269?book_show_action=true">Jul 07, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Apoorva" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Apoorva" href="/user/show/25605420-apoorva">Apoorva</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25605420-apoorva?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1689837269" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3067520677545494493"><a href='https://eternaldreamlander.wordpress.com/2019/01/27/death-note-by-tsugumi-ohba-and-takeshi-obata/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Read on blog</a><br/><br/>This will be the review for the whole series.<br/><br/>Let me preface this review by saying that ‘Death Note’ is one of my favorite mystery thriller series of all time, if not my favorite. I was introduced to it by my brother who basically forced me to watch the anime as he was a big fan of it; plus he wanted to get me into anime as he loved it and wanted me to share his hobby but I couldn’t get the appeal behind it. I remember we even had an argument about it.<br/><br/>I believed manga/anime is not rea</span>
  <span id="freeText3067520677545494493" style="display:none"><a href="https://eternaldreamlander.wordpress.com/2019/01/27/death-note-by-tsugumi-ohba-and-takeshi-obata/" rel="nofollow noopener">Read on blog</a><br /><br />This will be the review for the whole series.<br /><br />Let me preface this review by saying that ‘Death Note’ is one of my favorite mystery thriller series of all time, if not my favorite. I was introduced to it by my brother who basically forced me to watch the anime as he was a big fan of it; plus he wanted to get me into anime as he loved it and wanted me to share his hobby but I couldn’t get the appeal behind it. I remember we even had an argument about it.<br /><br />I believed manga/anime is not really my thing if you know what I mean. Guess what? I was utterly and irrevocably mistaken! He told me not to be judgemental about something unless I’ve tried it or at least made an effort to know about it. So, I did and I know, it’s kind of ridiculous to associate a trivial thing to something profound but for real, this experience has taught me to be open minded about things in general.<br /><br />‘Death Note’ revolves around Light Yagami, a high school student in Japan. He’s an extremely smart overachiever who excels at almost everything he does. Nothing is difficult for him and he’s bored out of his mind. On the other hand, we have Shinigami (God of Death) Ryuk who is also fed up in his Shinigami realm as there’s nothing much to do, so he decides to beat his boredom by dropping his ‘Death Note’ in the human realm.<br /><br />Light’s life changes immensely when one fateful day, he discovers a ‘Death Note’ lying in his schoolyard. It’s a notebook that allows you to kill any person whose name is written in it provided you know what they look like. At first, he dismisses the notebook thinking that it’s just a prank. But, he soon discovers that it’s legit when he decides to verify it by writing a person’s name in the notebook and that person ends up dying. Now, it seems like Light knows exactly what he wants to do: use the power of ‘Death Note’ to get rid of the evil in the world. Due to this, chaos ensues as the criminals start dropping dead mysteriously around the world.<br /><br />As the deaths of the criminals continue, people praise this mysterious entity and name him ‘Kira’ which means killer. A special task force is formed to find this peculiar killer who is able to kill people without leaving any clues behind. The task force is headed by an equally smart L, a widely famous detective whose name and identity are obscure. He openly challenges Light by claiming that he will find him and punish him. Therefore, begins the cat-and-mouse chase to see who can uncover other’s identity and bring justice in the world.<br /><br />It is one of the best-written mysteries incorporating a supernatural element. But, for me, the cherry on the cake was the conflict between the two main characters having different ideologies. On one side, we have Light who believes killing a person is justified as long as he deserves to die; a person who has committed a crime should be punished for it and death of that person means one less criminal and one more step towards creating a utopian society where only honest and hardworking people exist.<br /><br />On the other side, we have L who believes that it’s not anybody’s place to play God and create a society by cherry picking good people and eliminating bad people as he has no right or qualification to do so. Both Light and L are convinced that they’re justice and they’ll do anything to uphold their idea of justice. Hence, begins a battle of wits to defeat each other and ensure that justice prevails.<br /><br />Light and L are two of my absolute favorite characters of all times. Despite having contrasting beliefs, both are similar in many ways. Both of them are extremely smart, in fact, smarter than other people around them. That’s why they’re able to grasp each other’s perspective which causes a psychological war between them. It’s like playing house of cards; one wrong move and you’re caught. They may be rivals, but in each other, they find their equals which sort of creates a connection between them.<br /><br />L is an eccentric character who has shadows beneath his eyes, he is addicted to sweet things and he has a peculiar way of talking and sitting. He was absolutely adorable and he added a little lightness to the story. Similarly, Ryuk was another comical character who loves apples and his favorite catchphrase is: Humans are so interesting! Who knew God of Death could be this cool! He hangs out with Light and guides him and often annoys him. But, throughout the book, he remains neutral and enjoys the fruits of his labor! He might look terrifying but I assure you, he’s a sweetheart. I also loved the characters in police investigation team assisting L.<br /><br />The story takes place over the course of roughly ten years that begins with the appearance of Death Note in the human realm. A lot of characters get introduced as the story progresses and there are a lot of twists and turns that kept me hooked. I enjoyed it immensely. In the beginning, you find yourself rooting for Light but as the events unfold, you start leaning towards L and sometimes, find yourself shifting between two ideologies. I loved the ending as it shows that justice always prevails.<br /><br />So, what is justice? This brilliantly written story raises this important question and it makes you seriously think about this question. Is it ok to kill someone if their death won’t affect anyone? I see this same question being raised in the classic ‘Crime and Punishment’ by Fyodor Dostoevsky which is another book I loved which might’ve inspired Death Note. Also, what’s interesting about Death Note is that that creator’s identity is a closely guarded secret which is so interesting!<br /><br />Another question the Death Note raises is: are people inherently evil or is it the power that makes them so? I’m sure you’ve heard: With great power comes great responsibility. But, is it true that great power also gives the power to justify evil? Light’s sole purpose is getting rid of bad people by killing them which does not make him any better than those whom he killed. If he didn’t have the power, he wouldn’t have gotten a chance to kill so freely. That’s something to think about.<br /><br />All in all, Death Note will always be a favorite classic manga/anime series of mine and I highly recommend reading it!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3067520677545494493" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14337254491186177944"><b>Actual review:</b> 3.5<br/><br/><b>
  <i>“Death is equal.”</i>
</b><br/><br/>We have finally come to the end, and I am satisfied. It was a bit underwhelming, but it fulfilled a deep need that I wanted to see in black and white, so I have no criticisms regarding the ending. <br/><br/>Actually, that’s a lie. <br/><br/>After reading this series, I watched the anime, and I was surprised by how much I preferred the ending in the anime series compared to the manga.   <span id="freeText14337254491186177944" style="display:none"><b>Actual review:</b> 3.5<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“Death is equal.”</i>
</b><br /><br />We have finally come to the end, and I am satisfied. It was a bit underwhelming, but it fulfilled a deep need that I wanted to see in black and white, so I have no criticisms regarding the ending. <br /><br />Actually, that’s a lie. <br /><br />After reading this series, I watched the anime, and I was surprised by how much I preferred the ending in the anime series compared to the manga. There was a sense of poetic justice in what happened, and I found Light’s behaviour more in character than in the manga. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I recognise that dying brings out the worst in people but I didn’t understand how Light became such a desperate, sniveling coward at the end when he was always a fighter. He did try to get Ryuk to show him mercy, but I found the anime a better representation of everything we learned about him because even at the end, he was still arrogant. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />	♣ <b>Series Review:</b><br /><br />I <i>loved</i> this concept. I loved how each edition was like watching chess moves between two worthy opponents. I flew through the first few editions because they were addictively good. <br /><br />But then, things started to get repetitive. The same move was done by more and more people and the novelty was lost. I wish it had ended four or five editions ago. I would have rather wanted more from the series rather than find myself think, ‘Enough already’.<br /></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1144124719" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6028587562648547687">Underwhelming, I was expecting an epic showdown between Light and Near, instead them meeting was mostly cheesy and boring, and Light turned into such a pathetic and one dimensional character. Did really like the creepy-ish ending with Misa and the Kira followers though.<br/>Overall, the series was fairly enjoyable, it was only the last few instalments that let it down.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_560586845" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/560586845" />
    <a title="Emelie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4757979-emelie"><img alt="Emelie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533393759p2/4757979.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/560586845?book_show_action=true">Mar 13, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emelie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emelie" href="/user/show/4757979-emelie">Emelie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4757979-emelie?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer560586845" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8083795600713364460">Yes, I just finished the <i>Death Note</i> series.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380383635ra/741920.gif' width='300' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Guys, it's over. My god, it's over. What am I to do now? <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380413310ra/813630.gif' width='300' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Okay, let's get serious. I LOVED these books. It was amazing, such a wonderful read, and yes there were flaws and you could analyse the series to death and find so many things that could've been done better, but you know what? I enjoyed the whole idea of the shinigami and the Death Notes, the brilliant characters and inner struggles and dialouges so damn much that I am willing to look past the stu</span>
  <span id="freeText8083795600713364460" style="display:none">Yes, I just finished the <i>Death Note</i> series.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380383635ra/741920.gif" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Guys, it's over. My god, it's over. What am I to do now? <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380413310ra/813630.gif" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Okay, let's get serious. I LOVED these books. It was amazing, such a wonderful read, and yes there were flaws and you could analyse the series to death and find so many things that could've been done better, but you know what? I enjoyed the whole idea of the shinigami and the Death Notes, the brilliant characters and inner struggles and dialouges so damn much that I am willing to look past the stupidity of Misa. I am willing look past the steretypics on women, and the way Light treats Misa is part of his characters, I'm sorry but it's true. I don't have to like it, but it's okay because it helped creating these big plottwists and brilliant character development. Light is such a fascinating character because he represents a young man who has everything, who would have become a great detective, but who got hold of a notebook to kill people. His motives were good at first, but no one has the right to pass judgement on humanity. He became arrogant and full of himself, believing to be a god, and this proved to be the cause of his downfall. It was really very interesting to read and see how he developed as a character throughout the series, and how far he had fallen in the end. His final monolouge was brilliant and showed just how rotten he had become himself, because he was only human. <b>Light Yagami</b> is a brilliant character, possible one of my favourites of all time.<br><br>This ending... it was fantastic, now that I think about it. I'm really happy with this ending, and the final scenes, even if I was so shocked at first. I still think there are some lost threads in the story, e.g. I would've liked to know what had happened to Naomi Misora by the end of the series. Yes, yes, Light told her to kill herself and never be found, but I would've liked an ending to her story as well. She pretty much disappeared and was never found, so I would've liked to have closure. <br><br>Also, what happened to Light? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Ryuk wrote his name down in the notebook to die of a heartattack, which he did, but where did his soul go? I like to imagine that he became a Shinigami, because I can't really grasp that he is gone forever. Perhaps it is simply wishful thinking, but I can't imagine him being nothing. Or maybe that's the beauty of his death, how he accompanied all those he had killed in nothingness. Perhaps the beauty of his death is to prove that he is only human. He is not a god - Kira is not God - and thus like all humans he died and became nothing. No heaven or hell, just nothing. Yeah, that is beautiful.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380413310ra/813631.gif" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Of course, this was destined to be the saddest volume - after volume 7 at least - since it is the final one. Also, that ending... such a beautiful cliffhanger. Well, not exactly a cliffhanger, but that final shot with Misa... that was beautiful and sad and I want to know what happened after that! Ahhhh, I need more!<br><br>But seriously, I fucking loved this series. No, I still love it - I love this series. It was brilliant, I loved all the complicated dialouges, inner monolouges, all these sneaky planning and cleverness... It was so much, even if I did facepalm during some points as well. Not necessarily in this volume, but it happened. And oh my god that ending. That damn plot twist!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380413310ra/813632.gif" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Such a goddamn beautiful ending, and I loved that thing about Mello and Near, how they in the end worked together. I'm still not done mourning L yet, so I haven't really accepted Near yet... but I'm getting there. That ending was brilliant and I did not see it coming. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I was so sure Light had won! I was so god damn sure, I didn't know how he could lose. Of course, I knew from the beginning of the series that Light would someday fall, but I was so sure that he had won when he explained about the fake notebook and how he had had Mikami switch it and.. aaarrrghh! So good! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>I loved reading this series, I almost couldn't put them down. I read during my way to school, during recess, on the train back home, at home, I pretty much breathed <i>Death Note</i>. When the ticket controllers came on the train and disturbed my reading, or if someone disturbed me in school during recess, I was pretty much like this:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380413310ra/813633.gif" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Yeah. <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380413310ra/813634.gif" width="200" height="100" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And now it's over. I'm sorry, I can't let this go. BUT MY EMOTIONS! HOW COULD THEY! THEY CAN'T END THE SERIES. Actually I'm happy it has ended, because I'm not a big fan of extremely long series. Like <i>Bleach</i> or <i>Naruto</i>, I don't have the energy to focus on such long series for long. 12 books was enough, I'm happy. Now, if you excuse me, I'm going to go watch the anime, read all the Death Note novels and sulk, thank you very much.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380413310ra/813635.gif" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/377608.gif" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="8083795600713364460" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3465967652" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer2124210459440262095"><i>
  <b>Finis</b>
</i> !<br/><br/>An end to a long running, mother of all twists, battle of brain series - Death Note!<br/>It was fulfilling, sad and satisfying all at the same time!<br/><br/>The end result, though a bit predictable, also had a plot twist to it. Much like Tsugami's every other Death Note volume.<br/><br/>The evil just got worse and lost all his dignity whereas the Truth prevailed. Tsugumi had the readers running around in circles and waiting till the last moment to shove a bomb of a twist in the end!<br/>The entire series is a rea</span>
  <span id="freeText2124210459440262095" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>Finis</b>
</i> !<br /><br />An end to a long running, mother of all twists, battle of brain series - Death Note!<br />It was fulfilling, sad and satisfying all at the same time!<br /><br />The end result, though a bit predictable, also had a plot twist to it. Much like Tsugami's every other Death Note volume.<br /><br />The evil just got worse and lost all his dignity whereas the Truth prevailed. Tsugumi had the readers running around in circles and waiting till the last moment to shove a bomb of a twist in the end!<br />The entire series is a real battle of wits and it's quite impressive to deliver 12 full volumes of it!<br /><br />Light's character rapidly oscillates between Protagonist to Antagonist until the later volumes where the evil in him is clearly visible. Unfortunately, Ryuk's role in the later novels was too much undermined and infact unused. Even towards the end, his actions were deliberate and not much convincing.<br /><br />All in all, this was a really beautiful series to read &amp; I'd be missing now that it's over. <br /><br /><i>Recommended to all the folks who love plot twists!</i> </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer315767345" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18381524583178055327">Wow. What a way to close a series. Yes, it is mostly Near and Light standing around talking at each other, but hasn't that been the entire series so far? For a series with a death toll in the thousands, there's been very little action. It's all been a giant chess match with Light. And of course, he loses. His reaction to his loss isn't really surprising, even though it's startling, and it's one of those times that I love reading comics/manga. The words and the art feed off each other to make a m</span>
  <span id="freeText18381524583178055327" style="display:none">Wow. What a way to close a series. Yes, it is mostly Near and Light standing around talking at each other, but hasn't that been the entire series so far? For a series with a death toll in the thousands, there's been very little action. It's all been a giant chess match with Light. And of course, he loses. His reaction to his loss isn't really surprising, even though it's startling, and it's one of those times that I love reading comics/manga. The words and the art feed off each other to make a much bigger emotional impact than either could do alone. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[And I always thought, from the first volume, that Light's ultimate fate would be to have Ryuk write his name in his Death Note. I think at some point, Light started to think of Ryuk as his pet. But he told him at the beginning, he was just there for some entertainment. Even if he had won, I expect that Ryuk would have gotten bored eventually and written his name down anyways. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />As a whole, Death Note is very wordy and spends most of its time in various characters' head spaces. It isn't action packed, and even though it's "only" 12 volumes, it's still a fairly significant investment in time and headspace. If an extended battle of wits with multiple players sounds appealing, I absolutely recommend it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18381524583178055327" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6495958848884755131">Death Note is love. <br/>Death Note is life.<br/><br/>Okay, honestly though, now that I've finished the series I feel like ... lost. I don't know what to do with my life. My heart was pounding the entire time; I even found myself reading it out loud, and I was way to into mind you. My brother was likely in the other room really, really confused. Until he realized what I was reading, and even then the only thing stopping him from walking over here would be his inability to hear correctly as of this morning (bad</span>
  <span id="freeText6495958848884755131" style="display:none">Death Note is love. <br />Death Note is life.<br /><br />Okay, honestly though, now that I've finished the series I feel like ... lost. I don't know what to do with my life. My heart was pounding the entire time; I even found myself reading it out loud, and I was way to into mind you. My brother was likely in the other room really, really confused. Until he realized what I was reading, and even then the only thing stopping him from walking over here would be his inability to hear correctly as of this morning (bad cold, hallelujah for moi). Anyway, Death Note is truly one of the very best mangas out there. It's creative, and thrilling, and just all around amazing -- I don't even know how to explain my immense love for this series. Even if, as some of you may know (maybe?) I had to take a very, very lengthy break from it after the events that transpired in volume seven <s>still crying.</s> It feels almost unpredictable, and so unreal that it's real, and does a damn good job of screwing with your emotions. It's just amazing. Read it. Yay &lt;3 </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17012134030286756965"><i>
  <b>book 44 out of 75</b>
</i><br/><i>manga</i><br/><br/>What the hell just happened? That was literally so fast, I don't even know how to feel. It wasn't a bad ending by any means, and it isn't that it was unsatisfactory. It was just a little underwhelming. I truly believe that Light progressively and gradually became stupider throughout the last volumes.   <span id="freeText17012134030286756965" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>book 44 out of 75</b>
</i><br /><i>manga</i><br /><br />What the hell just happened? That was literally so fast, I don't even know how to feel. It wasn't a bad ending by any means, and it isn't that it was unsatisfactory. It was just a little underwhelming. I truly believe that Light progressively and gradually became stupider throughout the last volumes. I don't know, in the earlier volumes I had unwavering confidence in his ability to outwit &amp; manipulate others, but I began to have a lot of doubts at around the halfway mark of the series. Of course I'm aware that he was far from a perfect character, but I feel like he just lost his touch or something. And the ending felt so abrupt after having eleven volumes of Kira trying to build what he thought was this ideal world. By the end I didn't even know whose side I was on anymore.<br /><br />And there's also that complaint that I write in my every review of every volume about there not being a single intelligent / strong female character. The only female characters we saw throughout the entire series that was remotely important were Sayu, Light's mother, Misa, Takada, Lidner, Naomi Misora and that girl Light went out with at some point (I think her name was Yuri). AND NONE OF THEM HAD ANY INPUT TO THE STORY EXCEPT FOR BEING THERE, BEING USED BY LIGHT, OR KILLED OFF. NOT A SINGLE ONE OF THEM.<br /><br />I gotta admit that I'll miss Ryuk. Him and his apple addiction were so amusing to read about, and I feel like him, Light and Mello were my favorite characters by the end.<br /><br />And hello?? What was with that last chapter?! Is there a sequel or something???<br /><br />Overall series rating: 4 stars<br /><br />First four volumes were phenomenal. By the fifth and sixth I was completely lost. By this volume, the plot had become really repetitive and I was like, "Get it over with already." Still very enjoyable.<br /><br />➼ <i>
  <b>3.5 stars</b>

<div id="review_1360459582" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1360459582" />
    <a title="Sarah El Harake" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22667446-sarah-el-harake"><img alt="Sarah El Harake" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604026721p2/22667446.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1360459582?book_show_action=true">Aug 10, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah El Harake" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah El Harake" href="/user/show/22667446-sarah-el-harake">Sarah El Harake</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1360459582" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14520853337236827236"> This is the first time that I felt scared to watch the last episode of a series and to read the last book in a series too. It is because I knew how it is going to end and part of me did not want this ending or perhaps I did not want it to end yet. I mean it is obvious from how the events were progressing that the ending is going to be a just one. I am not saying that I wanted Light to live, it is just that I wanted him to die in a more dramatic way. Maybe the way it ended is perfect and there i</span>
  <span id="freeText14520853337236827236" style="display:none"> This is the first time that I felt scared to watch the last episode of a series and to read the last book in a series too. It is because I knew how it is going to end and part of me did not want this ending or perhaps I did not want it to end yet. I mean it is obvious from how the events were progressing that the ending is going to be a just one. I am not saying that I wanted Light to live, it is just that I wanted him to die in a more dramatic way. Maybe the way it ended is perfect and there is no other way to end it without giving the moral lesson it delivers. Light would never kill himself because he is too narcissistic to even think about it, so maybe Ryuk killing him after his identity gets discovered is actually the perfect ending. The moral lesson the series delivers is quite simply obvious: power corrupts. It is scary what we may do if we obtain any form of power when we aspire to be a god. Whom are we to judge each other and decide if the world is better without people who made bad choices? Light aimed at having a malfunctioning utopia; being good out of fear does not make someone really good. I think Light is the antagonist in the series. Mello is my favorite character because I think he is the true hero in the series because if it weren't for him sacrificing his life Kira would have never been caught. In addition to that he is often less appreciated than N and L are. <br /> Death Note is a must for everyone to read/watch. It is a classic in the manga/anime world and it is for those who seek a genius, full of suspense plot. </span>

Something which is rarely found in a graphic novel, err... a comic!<br /><br />.......<br /><br />The closing scenes depicted a group of people marching and gathering in a form of ritual with candles and hooded-robes, holding their hands in front of their chests full of hopes. <br /><br />Someone must punish those bad guys, the rotten people, the agents of decays in the society. If not one of the good guys, then it should be a third party. An omnipotent being who can overrule all of us.<br /><br />This hope happens to be our conventional and inevitable solution for the dilemma. In spite of the fact that the struggle between the bad and the good force is never-ending, it always feels good to have hopes. <br />Just like the condemned Sysiphus pretending to be happy and satisfied with his existence. <br /><br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_1991124892" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1991124892" />
    <a title="Trey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/58562374-trey"><img alt="Trey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1534072197p2/58562374.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1991124892?book_show_action=true">May 04, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trey" href="/user/show/58562374-trey">Trey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1991124892" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7188386580337272231">I honestly did not sympathize for Light Yagami. His cruelty towards Misa (My favorite character besides L) and Takada, I thought he was going to live so to be honest, I was expecting him to start liking either one of the two and form realistic feelings. But with Light becoming the unfeeling creature that he is, Misa was left in the dust and of course Takada died from the FIRE. Light's unfeeling, cold, unrealistic, godly, sucky, cruel, cold-blooded, two-timing, smart-to-be-dumb rear end (curse wo</span>
  <span id="freeText7188386580337272231" style="display:none">I honestly did not sympathize for Light Yagami. His cruelty towards Misa (My favorite character besides L) and Takada, I thought he was going to live so to be honest, I was expecting him to start liking either one of the two and form realistic feelings. But with Light becoming the unfeeling creature that he is, Misa was left in the dust and of course Takada died from the FIRE. Light's unfeeling, cold, unrealistic, godly, sucky, cruel, cold-blooded, two-timing, smart-to-be-dumb rear end (curse word). <br />First off, Mello's death in the beginning was honestly too soon and should have been relocated towards the ending somehow. I didn't understand the purpose of his character, although he was to be heir of L's, I felt he was unnecessary as we didn't see his character appear for long periods of time. Near on the other hand, I have to *smh* at the fact that he defeated Light. Like I said, I hate Light but I downright was not expecting Light to lose at all especially as he was talking to himself and how he predicted Near's actions and how it was too easy. What's weird is that throughout those pages, I was instantly thinking, this author is too unpredictable especially with Soichiro's and L's death (That hurt) and I kept asking, is Light about to fail. And he did.................You know what, I don't like Near. And I felt those pages with him playing with his toys were utterly dumb. <br />Anyway, did anyone think about Sayu and the mother, like, we just left the two in the dust? <br />Second, Ryuk, should have....he shouldn't have killed Light like that, that was cold-blooded and I was honestly thinking Ryuk would favor Light and kill off the others, I actually got excited and was like "Oh, the ending I was expecting, whoopee" until I saw Light was going to be receiving a heart attack. HOW DO YOU DEAL WITH THAT?!! And his meltdown was not at all expected, I didn't like seeing that side of Light as the entire time I kept encouraging myself that Light was going to rebound and throw out a witty comment and kill off everyone which I truly wanted. Aizawa was an annoying character that should have died and well Mikama is.....a disgrace. <br />Did I say, I love Misa's character, I honestly do, don't know why. But I felt she was constantly being placed on the backburner and constantly being used, which she wrongfully was. I wanted the series to end with Light and Misa running off in the sunset, Kira 1 and Kira 2 happily ever after. I don't mind her appearance on the last page though leading the cult. I loved that and it made me respect her more, gosh dang it. I only wish Misa would have been smart enough to realize Light never loved her, Ryuk even knew it!! <br />But we all know, what this review is really about..................In the ending of "Zero", in my list of Death Note's Saddest or Most Emotional Moments besides Light's dad dying, Light himself, Misa cutting her halved lifetime in half once more..............SHOOT, MISA's going to die in a short amount of time.............Light you suck. That made me angry though when Misa cut her lifetime in half again, so riled up. But the truly saddest moment of them all, my favorite, absolutely favorite character besides Misa, now that I think about it was L. Those first 7 manga, everybody has been saying and I thought about it as well, I honestly believe those 7 was just so unpredictable and satisfying and heart pounding, dramatic, the suspense, it was crazy. I guess the last 5 or so was disappointed because Light and Near was going back and forward on the huge screens and never really doing anything. But L was truly an answer, enemy to the protagonist that wasn't actually the antagonist. <br /><br />I mean, L, the guy who always kept eating sugar, sitting in his chair all crunched up, a finger in his mouth. Can you hate him?! And then to see him get killed all of a sudden. I honestly didn't think it was possible. I was crazed. *Sighs* Hurt me so bad. <br /><br />I don't know if I can say anything more besides, a job well done to the author and a job well done to L and Misa. Besides that, I'm going to go cry in bed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7188386580337272231" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1791169051" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1791169051" />
    <a title="Mit" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42022278-mit"><img alt="Mit" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1522148591p2/42022278.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1791169051?book_show_action=true">Oct 22, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mit" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mit" href="/user/show/42022278-mit">Mit</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1791169051" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8255039354464555728"><b>The Battle Ends Here!!!!Finally</b> <br/>I am gonna review the entire series in this final volume. What a series it was, what a journey it was from the beginning to the end. There was not a single chapter where it felt like the series is drifting away from the main plot line. It was building very nicely towards the final showdown. <br/>And finally we see the breakdown of a character whom I had almost considered an absolute genius. I had never thought that i would see Light's character breaking down at the end</span>
  <span id="freeText8255039354464555728" style="display:none"><b>The Battle Ends Here!!!!Finally</b> <br />I am gonna review the entire series in this final volume. What a series it was, what a journey it was from the beginning to the end. There was not a single chapter where it felt like the series is drifting away from the main plot line. It was building very nicely towards the final showdown. <br />And finally we see the breakdown of a character whom I had almost considered an absolute genius. I had never thought that i would see Light's character breaking down at the end like this. I am sure many were disappointed with the ending and yeah I am not Light Yagami Fan, so i was satisfied with the ending but I am also not Near's fan either.. It had to be L, but unfortunately this is how series turned out. There had to be sacrifices of characters to make any story look good and it just happened..<br />This Manga and also the Anime kept me on the edge of the seat till the end and I consider this as a masterpiece of any type of Movie,book or TV series I have witnessed.. <br /><i>So, let's see the character of Light Yagami</i><br />He is a student and a genius, he would have made a fine detective just like his father. His deduction skills and logical skills are at peak and despite of having everything in his life, he decides to become the god of this world with the help of a notebook, yeah that's right, a notebook. Just how far human needs can go? how much a human wants for happiness.. the greed and lust for the status and power, that is what Light yagami is all about.. <br />The series is over and I am just gonna think about what book i will read next, will it create the same excitement as Death note created? i do not know.. but it will take some special book to take me out of this fantasy world which Death Note created... </span>
  <a data-text-id="8255039354464555728" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2781960288" />
    <a title="Lashaan Balasingam (Bookidote)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43439266-lashaan-balasingam-bookidote"><img alt="Lashaan Balasingam (Bookidote)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1554145466p2/43439266.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2781960288?book_show_action=true">Apr 13, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lashaan Balasingam (Bookidote)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lashaan Balasingam (Bookidote)" href="/user/show/43439266-lashaan-balasingam-bookidote">Lashaan Balasingam (Bookidote)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43439266-lashaan-balasingam-bookidote?shelf=manga">manga</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43439266-lashaan-balasingam-bookidote?shelf=read-in-2019">read-in-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43439266-lashaan-balasingam-bookidote?shelf=digital">digital</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2781960288" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9546675532157926544">You couldn't ask for a better ending to this series than this volume. <br/><br/>A battle of ego, of pride and of justice. <br/><br/>There is a lot of info-dumping and of unnecessary exposition done by some of the key characters but I have to admit that it was something that was quite common throughout the series.<br/><br/>In the end, the series dives into some of the most intriguing questions, from life and death to right and wrong, and with the unique premise of killer books and geniuses going up against each other, it gave</span>
  <span id="freeText9546675532157926544" style="display:none">You couldn't ask for a better ending to this series than this volume. <br /><br />A battle of ego, of pride and of justice. <br /><br />There is a lot of info-dumping and of unnecessary exposition done by some of the key characters but I have to admit that it was something that was quite common throughout the series.<br /><br />In the end, the series dives into some of the most intriguing questions, from life and death to right and wrong, and with the unique premise of killer books and geniuses going up against each other, it gave this series the opportunity to push the ideas pretty far and reflect on them.<br /><br />While the first couple of volumes remain the best of the franchise, the series does have its lows here and then that could easily bore you if the story hadn't been so interesting from the start.<br /><br />The series will be missed. Time to revisit its live-action adaptations and novel spin-offs now.<br /><br />Yours truly,<br /><br />Lashaan | Blogger and Book Reviewer<br />Official blog: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://bookidote.com/">https://bookidote.com/</a></span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('NCYNvvoL2nWUVgUlha3EXLmckUjZVsTcUwg7pHa8gSWILn1A1Sc4l8Az4LhkCrsAPCD6YIhyVeUUIzR+Y+4SRQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('5V3U09U9yqdwtvCRaLzSHTYX/uvNqVXXC/V2EyDAiTRZVaQt+hEoRSTTFQyJG61Bs6uVw5yNxO5M3nnJNZIaVA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/5502079.Tsugumi_Ohba">About Tsugumi Ohba</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/5502079.Tsugumi_Ohba"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1476730775p3/5502079.jpg);'></div>

</a></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4815679621903122231">Tsugumi Ōba (Profile in Japanese: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/19876928.______' title='大場 つぐみ' rel='nofollow noopener'>大場 つぐみ</a>), born in Tokyo, Japan, is a writer best known for the manga Death Note. His/her real identity is a closely guarded secret. As stated by the profile placed at the beginning of each Death Note manga, Ōba collects teacups and develops manga plots while holding his knees on a chair, similar to a habit of L, one of the main characters of the series.<br/><br/>There is spe</span>
  <span id="freeText4815679621903122231" style="display:none">Tsugumi Ōba (Profile in Japanese: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/19876928.______" title="大場 つぐみ" rel="nofollow noopener">大場 つぐみ</a>), born in Tokyo, Japan, is a writer best known for the manga Death Note. His/her real identity is a closely guarded secret. As stated by the profile placed at the beginning of each Death Note manga, Ōba collects teacups and develops manga plots while holding his knees on a chair, similar to a habit of L, one of the main characters of the series.<br /><br />There is speculation that Tsugumi Ōba is a pen name and that he is really Hiroshi Gamō. Pointing out that in Bakuman the main character's uncle was a one-hit wonder manga artist who worked on a gag super hero manga, very similar to Gamō and Tottemo! Luckyman in all aspects. Also that the storyboards drawn by Ōba greatly resemble Tottemo! Luckyman in style.</span>
